    Cignacco 2012

    71 preterm infants between 24 0/7 weeks' and 32 0/7 weeks' PMA

    Repeated heel lances

    • Sucrose group (n = 24): 20% oral sucrose (0.2 mL/kg), ∼2 min before the heel lance. If the infant seemed to be in pain during the heel lance phase, up to 2 additional doses of sucrose were administered and noted in the study chart.

    • Sucrose + FT group (n = 23): FT was started at the beginning of the baseline phase, and sucrose was given 2 min before the heel lance.

    • FT group (n = 24): FT was started at the beginning of the baseline phase, and the infant was 'tucked' through all 3 phases.

    BPSN. Data collection occurred during:

    • baseline (before any manipulation);

    • heel lance (skin preparation, heel stick and haemostasis after blood was drawn); and

    • recovery (3 min after the heel lance).

    The BPSN contains 9 items: 3 physiologic (HR, RR and SpO2) and 6 behavioural (grimacing, body movements, crying, skin colour, sleeping patterns, consolation) items.

    3 phases (baseline, heel stick, recovery) of 5 heel stick procedures were videotaped for each infant.

    Mean, SD

    Sucrose with and without FT had pain‐relieving effects even in preterm infants of GA ≤ 32 weeks having repeated pain exposures. These interventions remained effective during repeated heel sticks across time. FT was not as effective.

    Data were included in RevMan analyses.

    Funding source: Swiss National Science Foundation and the following private

    foundations: Botnar Foundation, Basel;

    the Foundation of Nursing Science, Basel; the Foundation for Research in

    Neonatology, Zürich; the Marie Anna Foundation, Basel; and the Foundation

    for Sick Children, Basel

    Declaration of interest: The authors indicated they had no financial relationships relevant to this article to disclose.

    Codipietro 2008

    101 term infants

    Mean PMA:

    • sucrose group: 39.3 weeks; and

    • BF group: 39.4 weeks

    Heel lance

    • 1 mL 25% sucrose via syringe (n = 50)

    • BF prior to heel lance (n = 51)

    • Duration of first cry (s), percentage of crying time in first 2 min, and percentage of crying time during blood sampling

    • HR (beats/min) increase from baselines at 30 s following commencement of procedure

    • SpO2 decrease

    • PIPP during blood sampling, 2 min after heel lance

    • Adverse events

    Median, range

    Percentage of crying during first 2 min: BF group, 4% (range 0% to 100%) compared to sucrose, 45% (range 0% to 100%) (P < 0.0001)

    Percentage of crying during sampling: BF group, 8% (range 0% to 100%) compared to sucrose, 56.5% (range 0% to 100%) (P = 0.0003)

    Median increase in HR from baseline to 30 s after start of heel lance was lower in BF group (13 beats/min; range 12 beats/min to 54 beats/min) compared to sucrose group (22 beats/min; range 32 to 65) (P = 0.005)

    Median decrease in SpO2 from baseline to 30 s after start of heel lance was greater in sucrose group (−3%; range 30% to 1%) compared to BF group (−1%; range −14% to 2%) (P = 0.001)

    Median PIPP scores lower in BF group (3.0) compared to sucrose group (8.5) (P < 0.0001)

    No adverse effects were noted in any infant.

    Data could not be used in RevMan analyses.

    Gao 2018

    86 preterm infants born before 37 weeks

    Heel lance

    • Routine care (routine comfort through gentle touch when infants cried; n = 21)

    • NNS (n = 22) 2 min before and during recovery of heel lance

    • 1 mL sucrose (0.2 mL/kg of 20%; n = 21) 2 min before heel lance

    • 1 mL sucrose (0.2 mL/kg of 20%) + NNS (n = 22) 2 min before heel lance

    • PIPP score (during heel lance, 1 min after heel lance)

    • HR (baseline = 2 min before, during, 1 min after heel lance)

    • SpO2 (baseline = 2 min before, during, 1 min after heel lance)

    • Crying time (baseline = 2 min before, during, 1 min after heel lance)

    • Incidence of adverse events

      • Choking, coughing, vomiting, abdominal distension, oral infection, necrotising enterocolitis

      • Sustained tachycardia (HR > 200 beats/min), bradycardia (HR < 80 beats/min), tachypnoea (RR > 80 beats/min), dyspnoea (RR < 20 beats/min), or oxygen desaturation < 80% for > 15 s

      • hyperglycaemia

    Mean, SD

    The combination group had lower PIPP scores, HR, and crying time during the heel lance and recovery phase than the sucrose, NNS and routine care groups (P < 0.0001).

    The combination group had a higher SpO2 than all other treatment groups (P < 0.035).

    There were no differences in the HR and SpO2 between the sucrose, NNS and routine care groups.

    The sucrose group and NNS group had similar duration of crying, and the routine care group had the longest duration of crying of all treatment groups.

    3 episodes of vomiting (1 in the routine care group, 1 in the NNS group and 1 in the sucrose + NNS group) and 2 infants who had abdominal distension (1 in the sucrose + NNS group and 1 in the routine care group) were reported.

    Data were included in RevMan analyses.

    Funding source: National Natural

    Science Foundation of China (81703246), the Preponderant Discipline Project of Universities in Jiangsu Province, Nursing Science Open Fund of Nanjing University of Chinese Medicine (YSHL2016‐018), Top‐notch Academic Programs Project of Jiangsu Higher Education Institutions (PPZY2015C258) and Project of Nursing Science in Nanjing University of Chinese Medicine (NZYHLXPPJG2017‐54)

    Gibbins 2002

    190 preterm and term infants, mean GA 33.7 weeks, < 7 d PNA

    Heel lance

    2 min prior to heel lance:

    • sucrose + NNS group: 0.5 mL 24% sucrose via syringe to the anterior surface of the tongue followed by pacifier (n = 64);

    • sucrose group: 0.5 mL 24% sucrose without pacifier (n = 62); and

    • water + NNS group: 0.5 mL sterile water with pacifier (n = 64)

    • PIPP scores at 30 s and 60 s after heel lance

    • Incidence of adverse events

    Reported means, SD

    Mean PIPP scores at both 30 s (P < 0.001) and 60 s (P < 0.001) after heel lance favoured sucrose group and sucrose + NNS group. Post hoc Tukey tests showed infants who received sucrose + pacifier had lower PIPP scores after heel lance at 30 s (mean 8.16, SD 3.24) compared to infants receiving sucrose alone (mean 9.77, SD 3.04) (P = 0.007) or water + NNS (mean 10.19, SD 2.67 (P < 0.001). At 60 s after heel lance, PIPP scores were lower for sucrose + NNS group (mean 8.78, SD 4.03) compared to the sucrose alone group (mean 11.20, SD 3.25) (P = 0.005) and water + NNS group (mean 11.20, SD 3.47 (P = 0.007). No differences in PIPP scores were found between sucrose alone group or water + NNS group at both follow‐up times.

    Minor adverse effects were observed in 6 infants, none of which occurred in the sucrose + NNS group. 1 neonate who received water with NNS choked when the water was administered but stabilised within 10 s. 3 infants randomised to the sucrose group and 2 infants randomised to the water with NNS groups experienced oxygen desaturation when the study intervention (sucrose or water) was administered. Each neonate recovered spontaneously with no medical intervention required.

    Data were used in RevMan analyses.

    Funding source: Hospital for Sick Children, Toronto Ontario, Canada for the Research Training Award

    Declaration of interest: not specified

    Gormally 2001

    94 term newborns, mean GA 39.4 weeks, second or third day of life

    Heel lance

    • Water group: no holding and sterile water given by pipette (n = 21)

    • Sucrose group: no holding and 0.25 mL 24% sucrose solution given by pipette (n = 22)

    • Holding + water group: holding and sterile water given by pipette (n = 20)

    • Holding + sucrose group: holding and 0.25 mL 24% sucrose solution by pipette (n = 22)

    All solutions given 3 times at 30‐second intervals

    • Percentage of time crying 1 min, 2 min and 3 min after heel lance

    • Mean HR before intervention and 1 min, 2 min and 3 min after heel lance; mean vagal tone index before intervention and 1 min, 2 min and 3 min after heel lance

    • Pain concentration scores for facial activity before intervention and 1 min, 2 min and 3 min after heel lance

    Not reported

    Crying decreased over time (P < 0.001), but no interaction was noted for time with holding, taste or both. Effect of taste on crying (P < 0.05) favoured sucrose group. No effect of holding (P = 0.09). No interaction between taste and holding to reduce crying (P = 0.37). Effect of combined interventions was additive.

    Although no change in mean HR due to holding or sucrose as main effects, there was an interaction between holding and taste (P < 0.004), indicating synergistic effect that was also dependent on pre‐intervention HR (P < 0.004). No main effects noted for vagal tone; as with HR, effect of vagal tone was dependent on pre‐intervention vagal tone for both holding and taste interventions (P < 0.03). Pre‐intervention levels interacted to decrease HR and vagal tone in infants who had higher rates before interventions.

    Pain concatenation scores measuring facial expressions of pain decreased over time (P < 0.001). Only the effect of holding reduced pain scores (P < 0.02). No difference as to whether infant received sucrose (taste main effect P = 0.68)

    No data could be used in RevMan analyses.

    Funding source: Medical Research Council of Canada (MT‐13633), the Allan Ross Fellowship and the Lewis Sessenwein Academic Award

    Declaration of interest: not specified

    Haouari 1995

    60 term infants, 37 weeks' to 42 weeks' gestation, 1 d to 6 d of age

    Harrison 2003

    99 sick hospitalised infants

    Mean GA (SD):

    • sucrose group: 36.7 weeks (3.3); and

    • control group: 36.8 weeks (3.7)

    (Author provided data on a subset of infants from a larger study (n = 128) that fulfilled our inclusion criteria)

    Heel lance

    • 1 mL water (n = 46)

    • 1 mL 25% sucrose (n = 53)

    For infants weighing ≤ 1500 g, the dose was reduced to 0.5 mL.

    • Duration of cry until 5‐second pause; incidence and duration of crying time during the heel lance and squeeze and during the 3‐min recovery period

    • HR at baseline; heel lance; during heel lance; and 1 min, 2 min and 3 min post‐heel lance

    • SpO2 (%) at baseline; heel lance; during heel lance; and 1 min, 2 min and 3 min post‐heel lance

    • 4‐point subset of the NFCS (brow bulge, eye squeeze, nasolabial furrow, stretch mouth) at heel lance; during heel lance; and 1 min, 2 min and 3 min post‐heel lance

    Mean, SD (collected from authors)

    Mean (SD) length of first cry was higher in the water group (70.5 s (83.6 s)) compared to the sucrose group (46.8 s (63.1 s)). The sucrose group cried 57.1% of the procedure time compared to 58.8% in the water group. The mean (SD) total duration of cry during the heel lance was 84.7 s (68.8 s) in the sucrose group and 87.4 s (87.1 s) in the water group.

    The mean (SD) HR upon heel lance was 163.0 beats/min (17.9 beats/min) in the sucrose group and 159.5 beats/min (19.2 beats/min) in the water group. HR at 30 s from the beginning of the procedure was 175.4 beats/min (22.2 beats/min) and 172.8 beats/min (23.6 beats/min) in the sucrose and water groups, respectively. The HR in both groups decreased after the procedure to 152.1 beats/min (22.5 beats/min) in the sucrose group and 154.2 beats/min (29.1 beats/min) in the water group 2 min post‐heel lance.

    Results of SpO2 (%) were similar between the 2 groups.

    Mean (SD) facial scores were reduced at heel lance (2.74 (1.8)) in the sucrose group compared to the water group (2.94 (1.6)) (P = 0.02) and at 1 min (P = 0.04) and 2 min (P = 0.046) post‐heel lance. No differences occurred at 3 min post‐heel lance.

    Data were included in RevMan analyses.

    Lago 2020

    72 preterm infants admitted to the NICU (23 weeks to 36 + 6 weeks of gestation at birth) with PNA < 28 d or before reaching 40 weeks' corrected PMA

    Heel lance

    • Group (A): both syringes 1 and 2 contained sucrose (24%, 0.3 mL,0.07 g of sucrose each) for infant ≤ 1000 g or 0.5 mL for infants > 1000 g (0.12 g of sucrose each) (2 doses of sucrose) (n = 35)

    • Group (B): infants were given a dose of sucrose (24%, 0.3 mL or 0.5 mL) in syringe 1 and the same quantity of sterile water in syringe 2 (1 dose of sucrose) (n = 36)

    Infants also received NNS and FT.

    • PIPP at 30 s, 60 s and 120 s after heel prick; the heel pricks were also rated using other pain scales more feasible in the clinical practice and indicated in Italy for their use in newborn (FLACC: Faces, Legs, Activity, Cry and Consolability; indirect 10‐cm VAS; NIPS), to compare the performance of these pain scales with the gold standard PIPP

    • Adverse events

    Median, IQR

    No differences in PIPP scores was found

    between the groups: median PIPP values 4.0 (IQR 3.0 to 4.0) vs 3.0 (IQR 3.0 to 4.0) at baseline; 6.0 (IQR 5.0 to 10.0) vs 6.0 (IQR 4.0 to 8.5) at 30 s; 6.0 (IQR 4.0 to 7.0) vs 5.0 (IQR 4.0 to 8.5) at 60 s; and 5.0 (IQR 4.0 to 7.0) vs 5.0 (IQR 4.0 to 7.5) at 2 min, in the experimental and standard treatment groups, respectively (P = 0.9020). There was no correlation between PIPP scores and other pain scales.

    No adverse effects were reported (i.e. no episodes of desaturation or bradycardia or “choking”).

    Leng 2013

    560 term neonates, GA 37 weeks to 42 weeks; birthweight 2500 g to 4000 g; age 3 d to 28 d

    Heel lance

    • Boiled water

    • 10% glucose

    • 25% glucose

    • 50% glucose

    • 12% sucrose

    • 24% sucrose

    • 30% sucrose

    • Increase in HR (beats/min)

    • Decrease in SpO2 (%)

    • Pain levels (test not specified)

    • Adverse events

    Reported means and full ranges, not IQRs

    The average HR increase 3 min, 5 min and 10 min after procedure in the 25% and 50% glucose groups, 12% and 24% and 30% sucrose groups was lower than those in the placebo group (P < 0.01 or 0.05). The average HR increase 3 min after procedure in the sucrose groups was lower than that in the glucose groups (P < 0.01). At 3 min after heel lance, neonates who received 30% sucrose had lower average HR increase than those who received 12% and 24% sucrose (both P < 0.05). The average SpO2 decrease 3 min, 5 min and 10 min after procedure was lower than that in the placebo group (P < 0.01). The average SpO2 decrease 3 min after procedure in the sucrose groups was lower than that in the glucose groups (P < 0.01). The average pain score 3 min, 5 min and 10 min after procedure was lower than that in the placebo group (P < 0.01). The average pain score 3 min after procedure in the sucrose groups was lower than that in the glucose groups (P < 0.01).
    No adverse events reported

    We could not include in RevMan analyses data for 30% sucrose vs sterile water for increase in HR and decrease in SpO2 at 3 min after heel lance, as data were reported as means and full ranges.

    In addition, results were reported late at 3 min, 5 min and 10 min after heel lance.

    Leng 2015

    671 term neonates, GA 37 weeks to 42 weeks at birth; PNA 3 d to 28 d; birthweight 2500 g to 4000 g; Apgar score ≥ 8 at 5 min after birth; resting HR 120 beats/min to 140 beats/min; resting O2 saturation ≥ 95%; required neonatal congenital metabolism disease screening or blood glucose test

    Shallow (blood glucose test) and deep (congenital metabolism disease screening) heel lance

    • Sucrose group: 2 mL 24% sucrose administered to the infant’s mouth by syringe 2 min before the heel lance procedure

    • Sucrose + NNS group: 2 mL 24% sucrose administered as above, then a standard silicone newborn pacifier was placed into the infant’s mouth until the end of the process.

    • Sucrose + swaddling group: infants were swaddled with a cotton blanket, upper but not lower limb movements were restricted by the blanket, and then 2 mL 24% sucrose were administered as above. The lower limbs were swaddled immediately after the heel lance procedure until the end of the process.

    • Sucrose + NNS + swaddling group: infants were swaddled with a cotton blanket, upper but not lower limb movements were restricted by the blanket, then 2 mL 24% sucrose administered as above, then a standard silicone newborn pacifier was placed into the infant’s mouth, the lower limbs were swaddled immediately after the heel lance procedure until the end of the process.

    • Revised NFCS

    • Increase in HR (%)

    • Decrease in SpO2 (%)

    • Factor analysis

    • Mean and SD

    A synergistic analgesic effect was observed between the sucrose + NNS and sucrose + swaddling groups in both the shallow (P = 0.015) and deep heel lance (P = 0.007) procedure. The sucrose + NNS + swaddling group exhibited the lowest pain score. For the deep heel lance procedure, the sucrose + NNS group had a lower increase in HR percentage and decrease in SpO2 (%) than the sucrose group (P = 0.000, P = 0.001), while this difference was not observed in the shallow heel lance procedure. No difference was found between the sucrose and sucrose + swaddling groups, in terms of different physiological parameters;

    NNS and swaddling had synergistic effects on pain relief when used with oral sucrose. For the deep heel lance procedure, oral sucrose combined with NNS and swaddling provided the best pain relief effect.

    For the shallow heel lance procedure, addition of NNS and swaddling did not improve the effects.

    Data could not be used in RevMan analyses.

    Funding source: National Key Clinical Specialist Construction Program

    of China, No [2013]544 and Medical Research Funding of Health Bureau of Chongqing, No [2011‐1‐071]

    Declaration of interest:

    none declared

    Liaw 2013

    110 infants (PMA 26.4 weeks to 37 weeks)

    Heel lance

    • Sucrose intervention: 0.2 mL to 2.0 mL 20% sucrose fed through a syringe 2 min before the heel‐lance procedures depending on the infant’s PMA (PMA 26 weeks to 28 weeks: 0.2 mL; PMA 28.1 weeks to 30 weeks: 0.5 mL; PMA 30.1 weeks to 32 weeks: 1 mL; PMA 32.1 weeks to 37 weeks: 1.5 mL; PMA > 37 weeks: 2.0 mL)

    • NNS intervention: NNS via a standard silicone newborn pacifier to stimulate sucking 1 min before touching the foot to initiate heel‐lance procedures

    • FT intervention: infants were in a flexed posture and gently held by the intervener’s warm hands without strongly restraining the infant’s head and body, one hand on the infant’s head, and the other on the trunk.

    The 3 interventions outlined above were used in different combinations:

    • NNS + FT (n = 22);

    • FT + sucrose (n = 21);

    • NNS + sucrose (n = 21);

    • NNS + sucrose + FT (n = 23); amd

    • control: routine care (n = 23).

    Infants’ behavioural states (quiet sleep, active sleep, transition state, active awake, quiet awake, fussing or crying)

    Graph form, CI, rate ratio and SE

    Infants receiving NNS + sucrose + FT or NNS + sucrose experienced
    52.8% (P = 0.023) and 42.6% (P = 0.063) more quiet‐sleep occurrences than those receiving routine care after adjusting for phase, baseline states, nontreatment sucking during baseline and recovery, positioning, and infants’ characteristics. Infants receiving FT + sucrose, NNS + sucrose, NNS + sucrose + FT and NNS + FT experienced 77.3% (P < 0.001), 72.1% (P = 0.008), 51.5% (P = 0.017) and 33.0% (P = 0.105) fewer occurrences of fussing or crying, respectively, than those receiving routine care after adjusting for related factors

    No data could be used in RevMan analyses.

    Ramenghi 1999

    30 preterm infants, GA 32 weeks to 36 weeks, PNA > 24 h

    Heel lance

    • 25% sucrose solution (volume not reported) given via syringe into the mouth or via NG tube 2 min prior to first heel lance (n = 15), and via the alternate route for the second heel lance within 48 h

    • Sterile water given via syringe into the mouth or via NG tube 2 min prior to first heel lance and for the second heel lance the alternate route within 48 h (cross‐over design, n = 15)

    The cross‐over concerned mode of delivery of the solution: intraorally or via NG tube.

    Infants stayed in their original group assigned to receive either sucrose or sterile water.

    • Percentage of time crying over 5 min after sampling

    • Behavioural scores (4 facial expressions and the presence of cry) at 1 min, 3 min and 5 min after the lance for a total behavioural score

    Median, IQR

    Median percentage of time crying in intra‐oral water group was 22% (IQR 10.6% to 40%) and 27% (IQR 11.6% to 47%) for infants in NG tube water group. Median percentage of time crying in intra‐oral 25% sucrose group was 6% (IQR 0.6% to 15%) and 18.3% (IQR 11.6% to 41.6%) in NG tube 25% sucrose group.

    Reduction in crying time (P = 0.006) was noted in the 25% sucrose group compared with water group when infants received 25% sucrose intra‐orally, not via NG‐tube route. For infants in 25% sucrose group, a reduction in crying time was noted (P = 0.008) when solution was given intra‐orally compared to NG tube route.

    Behavioural scores for the intra‐oral water group were 9 (IQR 6 to 12) and 10 (IQR 6 to 14) for NG tube water group. Behavioural scores for intra‐oral 25% sucrose group were 5 (IQR 3 to 6) and 9 (IQR 8 to 10) for NG tube sucrose group. Reduction in behavioural scores was noted in 25% sucrose group (P = 0.002) compared with water group when infants received 25% sucrose intra‐orally but not via NG route. For infants in 25% sucrose group, there was a reduction in behavioural score (P = 0.001) when solution was given intra‐orally compared to via NG tube.

    Cross‐over design: data from the first assignment prior to cross‐over were presented. These data were not used in RevMan analyses.

    245 neonates, 24 weeks' to 42 weeks' GA at birth and < 30 d of life or < 44 weeks' GA

    Heel lance

    All interventions given 2 min before heel lance

    • 0.1 mL 24% sucrose (n = 81)

    • 0.5 mL 24% sucrose (n = 81)

    • 1.0 mL 24% sucrose (n = 83)

    • PIPP‐R at 30 s and 60 s

    • Incidence of adverse events (HR > 240 beats/min or HR < 80 beats/min for > 20 s; SpO2 < 80% for > 20 s; no spontaneous respirations for > 20 s; and choking/gagging)

    Mean, SD

    Mean (SD) PIPP‐R scores at 30 s were 6.9 (3.5), 6.8 (3.2) and 6.7 (3.4) for 0.1 mL, 0.5 mL and 1.0 mL, respectively. There were no differences in PIPP‐R score between treatment groups at 30 s (P = 0.97) and at 60 s (P = 0.93).

    There were 5 adverse events reported: 3 infants experienced gagging, 1 had an HR < 80 beats/min and another developed 80% SpO2 following sucrose administration. There were no differences in proportion of adverse events between the intervention groups (P = 0.62), and all resolved spontaneously.
    No data could be used in RevMan analyses.

    Funding source: The Canadian Institutes of Health Research (MOP‐126167)

    Declaration of interest:

    the authors declared that they had no competing interests.

    Thakkar 2016

    180 full‐term neonates, birthweight > 2000 g and age > 24 h

    Heel lance

    • 2 mL 30% sucrose (n = 45)

    • 2 mL 30% sucrose + NNS (n = 45)

    • NNS (n = 45)

    • No intervention (n = 45)

    • PIPP

    • Total crying time

    • Adverse events

    Median, IQR

    Median (IQR) PIPP score was 3 (2 to 4) in the sucrose + NNS group compared with 7 (6.5 to 8) in the sucrose only group, 9 (7 to 11) in the NNS group and 13 (10.5 to 15) in the no intervention group. The sucrose + NNS group had a decrease in the median PIPP score compared with other groups (P = 0.000). Median PIPP score decreased with any intervention compared with no intervention (P = 0.000).

    A total of 5 episodes of adverse events were reported: 1 neonate each in the sucrose group, the NNS group and the sucrose + NNS group desaturated, and 2 neonates desaturated in the no intervention group.

    No data were used in RevMan analyses.

    Funding source: not specified

    Declaration of interest:

    the authors declared no conflict of interest.

    Tutag Lehr 2015

    56 term infants ≤ 7 d old: appropriate for GA

    Heel lance

    • 2.0 mL 24% sucrose orally (n = 29)

    • Sterile water orally (n = 27)

    • NIPS

    • Mean SBF

    • SBF

    • PU measured by LDI during heel lance

    • HR

    • RR

    • SpO2 (%)

    • Adverse events

    Mean, SE, median, IQR

    Mean SBF and median NIPS scores immediately post‐heel lance were lower in sucrose‐treated infants (SBF: 167.9 PU ± 15.5 PU vs 205.4 PU ± 16.0 PU, P = 0.09; NIPS: 1 (IQR 0 to 4) vs 3 (IQR 0 to 6), P = 0.02), although there was no difference in mean SBF. During heel lance, NIPS score was predictive of SBF. An increase of 1 in NIPS score was associated with 11‐PU increase in SBF (R = 0.21; P = 0.09) for sucrose and 16‐PU increase for placebo‐treated infants (R = 0.20; P = 0.014).

    Increased SBF assessed by LDI is a pain response among term neonates following routine heel lance that was not completely attenuated by oral sucrose administration. Increased SBF is associated with NIPS scores. Sucrose analgesic efficacy evidenced by decreased NIPS scores for the sucrose group. Association of SBF with NIPS scores suggests LDI is potentially useful for assessing newborn procedural pain.

    SEs were transformed to SDs and were used in RevMan analyses for SBF.

    For HR, RR and SpO2, results were presented as means and SDs and were used in RevMan analyses.

    Assessed adverse events including

    gagging, choking and vomiting, and only 1 infant in the sucrose group was noted to experience a mild episode of 'spitting up'.

    Funding source: The Gerber Foundation, Fremont, Michigan

    Declaration of interest: The authors

    declared no conflict of interest.

    Velumula 2020

    94 neonates born between 30 1/7 weeks' and 36 6/7 weeks' GA

    Heel lance

    • 0.5 mL 24% sucrose (n = 47)

    • 2 mL expressed breast milk via syringe (n = 47)

    Infants in both groups also received swaddling 2 min prior to scheduled heel lance.

    • PIPP‐R scores at baseline; during the procedure; and at 30 s, 60 s, 90 s and 120 s postprocedure, assessed in real time by two investigators. Final pain score was determined by calculating the average of the two assessors' scores.

    • Adverse events

    • Mean, SD

    • Median, IQR

    PIPP‐R scores during procedure ranged from 5 to 12 in the two groups, with a mean (SD) score of 8.3 (1.3). PIPP‐R scores at 30 s and 60 s post‐procedure ranged from 0 to 6 and 0 to 5 with mean (SD) of 4.14 (0.98) and 1.27 (1.88) at 30 s and 60 s, respectively. All infants reached their baseline score of 0 by 90 s post‐procedure. PIPP‐R scores at 60 s were lower in the breast milk group compared to sucrose group. No differences were noted in PIPP‐R scores during the procedure (P = 0.17) and at 30 s post‐procedure (P = 0.39). PIPP‐R scores at 60 s post‐procedure were higher in the sucrose group compared to breast milk group (P < 0.01).

    No adverse events were noted in any infant in both groups.

    Funding source: Institutional grant from Sarnaik Endowment Grant, Detroit Medical Center

    Declaration of interest: the authors declared no competing interests.

    Yilmaz 2010

    120 infants, GA 37 weeks to 42 weeks

    Mean GA (SD):

    • control group (n = 30): 39.67 weeks (0.80 weeks);

    • mother’s milk group (n = 30): 39.10 weeks (1.03 weeks);

    • sucrose group (n = 30): 39.10 weeks (0.71 weeks); and

    • pacifier group (n = 30): 39.20 weeks (0.93 weeks)

    Heel lance

    • Control group: infants lay in their mothers’ lap; no interventions were made before the painful procedure

    • Mother's milk group: 2 mL mother’s milk administered 2 min before the procedure by using an oral syringe and avoiding contact of the syringe with the mouth and lips

    • Sucrose group: 2 mL 20% sucrose via a syringe as above, 2 min before the procedure

    • Pacifier group: given a pacifier

    • NIPS score

    • HR

    • RR

    • Crying time

    Mean, SD

    No differences in HR and SpO2 between groups

    After the procedure, the mean crying time of the sucrose group was shorter than those of the other groups. Comparing the crying times of the control and experimental groups according to the procedure time showed no differences between the values before and during the procedure (F = 1.50, P > 0.05); (F = 2.43, P > 0.05).

    Before the procedure, the lowest NIPS mean was in the sucrose group, and the highest NIPS mean was in the pacifier group. During the procedure, no differences were found between the groups for NIPS means (P > 0.05). After the procedure, the sucrose group showed the lowest response to pain, while the mother's milk group had the highest response. Comparing the NIPS means of the control and experimental groups according to the procedure times, differences were found between the groups for values obtained before and after the procedure (F = 3.49, P < 0.05); (F = 6.71, P < 0.05).

    Outcome data were presented according to different procedure times, and no data could be included in RevMan analyses.

    Ogawa 2005

    100 healthy full‐term infants:

    • Heel lance + water group: GA 40 weeks (range 38 weeks to 42 weeks)

    • Heel lance + sucrose group: GA 39 weeks (range 37 weeks to 41 weeks)

    • Venipuncture + water group: GA 39 weeks (range 37 weeks to 41 weeks)

    • Venipuncture + sucrose group: GA 39 weeks (range 37 weeks to 41 weeks)

    Heel lance or venipuncture

    2 min before procedure:

    • heel lance + 0.1 mL sterile water on infant's tongue via syringe (n = 25);

    • heel lance + 0.1 mL 50% sucrose on infant's tongue via syringe (n = 25);

    • venipuncture + 0.1 mL sterile water on infant's tongue via syringe (n = 25); and

    • venipuncture + 0.1 mL 50% sucrose on infant's tongue via syringe (n = 25).

    Duration of first cry (s), first crying time/total procedure time (%) and the ratio of crying to no crying

    NFCS score:

    • 1 min after oral administration of water or sucrose;

    • disinfection of skin before heel lance or venipuncture;

    • during skin puncture;

    • during blood sampling;

    • during compression to stop bleeding;

    • during application of plaster; and

    • 1 min after application of plaster.

    Reported medians, range and mean, SD

    Reported in graph form, median and IQR

    Reduction in duration of first cry in heel lance group given sucrose compared to heel lance alone (P < 0.001)

    Reduced NFCS scores in sucrose group during heel lance (median 47, IQR 31 to 60) and during compression to stop bleeding (median 32, IQR 8 to 54) compared to the water group (median 58, IQR 54 to 65; median 52, IQR 41 to 61, respectively) (P < 0.001)

    Sucrose did not reduce NFCS scores during or after venipuncture

    We included data for sucrose vs water for heel lance and for venipuncture for duration of first cry.

    Gaspardo 2008

    33 preterm infants, median PMA 30 weeks

    Venipuncture, arterial puncture, heel lance, intravenous cannulation, endotracheal tube introduction, endotracheal tube suctioning, gavage insertion for feeding, removal of electrode leads and tape

    On day 1, no treatment was given to any neonate in order to collect baseline data. After that, on days 2 to 4 before every minor painful procedure, infants received either:

    • sucrose (n = 17): 0.5 mL/kg 25% sucrose; or

    • water (n = 16): 0.5 mL/kg sterile water.

    Pain was assessed over 4 d during morning blood collection (heel lance).

    Incidence of cry (percentage of neonates crying), HR (percentage of neonates with HR ≥ 160 beats/min),

    NFCS (percentage of neonates with score ≥ 3), Activated Behavioural State (percentage of neonates with score ≥ 4). The assessment was divided into 5 phases: baseline antisepsis, puncture, dressing and recovery. The neonates’
    facial activity (NFCS), behavioural state and HR were evaluated.

    No means or SDs reported;

    NFCS results reported in graph form only

    The data analysis used cutoff scores for painful and distressful responses. There were fewer sucrose‐group neonates with facial actions signalling pain than water‐group neonates in puncture phase and in antisepsis phase. There were fewer sucrose‐group neonates crying during antisepsis phase, puncture phase and dressing phase. There was no difference between groups for physiological response. The efficacy of sucrose was maintained for pain relief in preterm neonates, with no side effects.

    Data could not be used in RevMan analyses.

    No side effects of using sucrose were detected.

    Funding source: This study was supported by the FAPESP,

    the CNPq, and the FAEPA

    Declaration of interest: not specified

    Johnston 2002

    103 infants:

    • sucrose group: mean PMA 28.18 weeks (1.72 weeks); and

    • water group: mean PMA 28.05 weeks (2.06 weeks).

    Every time the infant was to undergo an invasive (e.g. heel lance, intravenous cannulation, arterial puncture, injection) or noninvasive but presumably uncomfortable procedure (e.g. endotracheal tube suctioning, tape or
    lead removal, gavage insertion for feeding), the infant received sucrose or water.

    • Sucrose group (n = 51): 0.1 mL 24% sucrose in sterile refrigerated syringe

    • Water group (n = 52): 0.1 mL water in sterile refrigerated syringe

    The solution was in a syringe and administered into the infant’s mouth at the beginning of the procedure, 2 min into the procedure and another 2 min into the procedure. If the procedure was > 15 min, up to another 3 doses (0.1 mL each) were to be given 2 min apart.

    Neurobehavioural development was assessed by the subscales of alertness and orientation and motor development and vigour of the NAPI, SNAP and NBRS.

    SNAP was measured for each 24‐hour period during the study week, and NBRS was measured at 2 weeks’ PNA and at discharge.

    Beta, CI (multiple regression)

    On the basis of analysis of covariance with PMA at birth and the number of invasive procedures as covariates, there were no group differences (between sucrose and water) for any of the secondary outcomes of NBRS at 2 weeks' PNA (P = 0.426) or at discharge (P = 0.965). In the sucrose group only, a higher number of sucrose doses predicted lower scores on motor development and vigour and on alertness and orientation at 36 weeks' PNA, lower motor development and vigour at 40 weeks' PNA, and higher NBRS at 2 weeks' PNA. A higher number of invasive procedures was predictive of higher NBRS both times in the water group.

    No differences were found between the sucrose and water groups for NAPI.

    Data could not be used in RevMan analyses.

    Funding source: Fonds de la Recherche en

    Sante du Quebec (961297‐104), the IWK Foundation, and Health

    Declaration of interest: not specified

    Taddio 2008

    240 newborn infants born to nondiabetic and diabetic mothers, PMA ≥ 36 weeks

    3 heel lances, venipuncture and IM vitamin K injection; multiple painful stimuli

    • 2 mL 24% sucrose given to infants of nondiabetic mothers (n = 60)

    • 2 mL 24% sucrose given to infants of diabetic mothers (n = 60)

    • 2 mL sterile water given to infants of nondiabetic mothers (n = 60)

    • 2 mL sterile water given to infants of diabetic mothers (n = 60)

    PIPP scores overall, during IM injection, during venipuncture and during all 3 heel lances

    Safety

    Mean, SD, 95% CI

    Overall PIPP scores were lower among newborns given sucrose (mean 6.8, SD 2.9) compared to water (mean 8.1, SD 2.5) (MD −1.3, 95% CI −2.0 to −0.6; P < 0.001).

    PIPP scores during IM injection did not differ between the sucrose and water group for nondiabetic (P = 0.10) or diabetic mothers (P = 0.15).

    PIPP scores during venipuncture were lower among infants of nondiabetic mothers who received sucrose compared to water (mean score 5.7, 95% CI 4.7 to 6.7 vs mean score 8.9, 95% CI 7.9 to 9.9; P < 0.001). Similar results were found amongst infants of diabetic mothers (sucrose: mean score 6.8, 95% CI 5.7 to 7.9 vs water: mean score 9.2, 95% CI 8.4 to 10.1; P < 0.001).

    During the first 3 heel lances, newborns from diabetic mothers receiving sucrose or water did not have different PIPP scores.

    Results for different painful stimuli were reported separately.

    Data could be used in RevMan analyses.

    Funding source: CIHR grant (MCT 63143) and a Sick Kids Foundation

    graduate student Research Training Competition Award

    Competing interests: none declared

    CI: confidence interval; CIHR: Canadian Institutes of Health Research; CNPq: National Council of Science and Technology Development; FAEPA: Foundation for Support of Teaching, Research and Assistance of the University Hospital of Clinics; FAPESP: Foundation for Support of Research in the State of São Paulo, Brazil; HR: heart rate; IM: intramuscular; MD: mean difference; NAPI: Neurobehavioral Assessment of the Preterm Infant; NBRS: Neuro‐Biological Risk Score; NFCS: Neonatal Facial Coding System; PIPP: Premature Infant Pain Profile; PMA: postmenstrual age; PNA: postnatal age; SD: standard deviation; SNAP: Score for Neonatal Acute Physiology
